Place the lamb in a large freezer bag. Add marinade ingredients, seal and refrigerate for at least 2 hours, or overnight.<\/p>\n<p>2. Preheat the grill to medium-high heat.<\/p>\n<p>3. Remove the lamb from the marinade and wipe off any excess with paper towels.<\/p>\n<p>Combine all the dry spices.<\/p>\n<p>Unfold the lamb, drizzle with a little olive oil, and sprinkle well with the mixed spices.<\/p>\n<p>Grill for about 15 minutes, then flip and cook until the lamb is medium rare, and charred on outside, 12 to 15 minutes more. The internal temperature should be 145F.<\/p>\n<p>Remove the lamb from the grill, tent with foil, and let rest for 10 to 12 minutes, then carve it across the grain into thin slices.<\/p>\n<p>4. Serve with Mint Mojo Sauce.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p><strong>Mint Mojo Sauce:<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>1. Combine the ingredients in a blender and process until smooth. Tip:<\/strong> The glaze can be made 2 to 3 days in advance, and you can score and glaze the ham the night before and refrigerate until ready to cook.<\/p>\n<p>1. Preheat the oven to 350F<\/p>\n<p>2. Make diagonal cuts in the ham 1 1\/2 to 2 inches deep, then make cuts across the first ones to form the classic &#8220;diamond&#8221; pattern.<\/p>\n<p>Press a whole clove into the center of each diamond.<\/p>\n<p>Place the ham on a rack in a large roasting pan. Add 1 cup of water to the pan to keep the drippings from burning. Bake for 1 1\/2 hours.<\/p>\n<p>3. Meanwhile, to make the glaze, heat the olive oil in a large saut\u00e9 pan over medium heat. Add the onion and garlic and saut\u00e9\u00a0until the onion is translucent, about 2 to 3 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Remove the pan from the heat and carefully add the cognac (the alcohol can flame up). Return the pan to the heat and cook to reduce for 2 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Star in the mustards, pineapple juice, apple juice, brown sugar, and honey and season to taste with salt and pepper.<\/p>\n<p>Turn the heat to low and cook for 15 to 20 minutes, or until the mixture has reduced by a third, stirring occasionally. Set aside.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p><strong>To Make the Salsa:<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>1. Heat an oiled grill pan over medium-high heat.<\/p>\n<p>Grill the pineapple and mango slices until they&#8217;re grill-marked and caramelized &#8211; 2 to 3 minutes per side.<\/p>\n<p>Remove and let cool, then cut the fruit into 1\/2-inch dice. Toss in a large bowl with the jalape\u00f1o, onion, olive oil and lemon juice.<\/p>\n<p>Season with salt and pepper to taste. Set aside.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p>Liberally apply the mustard glaze to the ham and bake for 30 minutes, or until the glaze begins to turn brown and caramelize.<\/p>\n<p>Remove the ham from the oven, cover with foil, and let rest for 10 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Slice and serve with the salsa.<\/p>\n","parent":null,"link":"http:\/\/www.guyfieri.com\/recipes\/jimbos-hambo-with-fruit-salsa\/","date":"2015-04-02T04:03:44","modified":"2015-04-02T04:04:02","format":"standard","slug":"jimbos-hambo-with-fruit-salsa","guid":"http:\/\/www.guyfieri.com\/?post_type=recipes&#038;p=5556","excerpt":"<p>Makes: 8 Servings Time:\u00a0About 3 hours You&#8217;ll Need: Oven, Stovetop, Grill Pan, Large Roasting Pan with Rack Prep-Ahead Tip: The glaze can be made 2 to 3 days in advance, and you can score and glaze the ham the night before and refrigerate until ready to cook. 1. Taste and season as needed.<\/p>\n<p>Generously butter a 9 by 9-inch baking pan. Pour the polenta onto the pan and let rest at room temperature to cool. Pariser","first_name":"Becca","last_name":"Pariser","nickname":"becca","slug":"becca","URL":"","avatar":"http:\/\/1.gravatar.com\/avatar\/a64ab12f1a2e03c57e5ed3daae0819d0?s=96","description":"","registered":"2014-01-22T18:04:20+00:00","meta":{"links":{"self":"http:\/\/www.guyfieri.com\/wp-json\/users\/9","archives":"http:\/\/www.guyfieri.com\/wp-json\/users\/9\/posts"}}},"content":"<p>Preheat the oven to 350 degrees F.<\/p>\n<p>Combine the panko bread crumbs and milk together and set aside.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Grind the Meat:<\/strong> Cut the sirloin and brisket into 1-inch cubes. Arrange on a baking sheet and transfer to the freezer for 15 to 20 minutes to firm up (this will make the grinding cleaner and easier).<\/p>\n<p>Follow the directions on your meat grinder attachment (bench top mixer or food processor) for grinding meat and gradually press each piece into the grinder. Cover the bowl of ground beef with plastic and set aside in fridge until ready to use.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Prepare the Meatloaf:\u00a0<\/strong> In a large saute pan over medium-high heat saut\u00e9 the onions, carrots, celery, peppers and garlic in the olive oil. Cook for about 5 minutes or until translucent. Add the oregano, cumin and chile de arbol and cook for another 2 minutes. Remove from the heat, transfer to a large bowl and allow to cool.<\/p>\n<p>Once the mixture is cool, add the ground beef, chorizo, milk-soaked panko, egg, corn and beans. Mix until just combined making sure not to overwork the meat.\u00a0 Season with salt and pepper.<\/p>\n<p>Transfer the mixture to a sheet tray lined with parchment paper. Free form the mixture into a flattened loaf shape.<\/p>\n<p>Bake for 45 minutes to 1 hour or until the internal temperature reads 160 degrees F.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Make the Avocado Crema:<\/strong> In a food processor, combine the avocado, sour cream, salt, pepper and lime juice. Keep in the refrigerator until ready to use<\/p>\n<p><strong>Make the Pesto:<\/strong> In a food processor, combine the cilantro, parsley, garlic, cumin, salt, pepper and toasted pepitas. Pulse until combined. Continue pulsing and slowly drizzle in the olive oil. Transfer the mixture to a bowl and fold in the cotija cheese and grated parmesan. Set aside.<\/p>\n<p>When the meatloaf is done, remove from the oven and immediately spread some of the pesto over the top of the loaf (the warmth from the loaf will heat the pesto and make it aromatic, and it will soak into the loaf.\u00a0 Tent with foil to rest for about 10 minutes.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Fry the Tortilla Strips:<\/strong> heat 2 inches of canola oil over medium-high heat to 350 degrees F.\u00a0 Finely slice the tortilla strips and fry in small batches until golden and crispy \u2013 about 2 to 3 minutes.\u00a0 Drain and season lightly with salt.<\/p>\n<p><strong>To serve:<\/strong> Slice the meatloaf into thick slices and serve with grilled polenta squares (see recipe below). Top with a dollop of cilantro pesto, a drizzle avocado crema and topped with crispy tortilla strips.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p>Yield: 6 to 8 servings<\/p>\n<p>Prep Time: 30 minutes<\/p>\n<p>Cook Time: 1 hour<\/p>\n<p>Inactive Prep Time: 10 minutes<\/p>\n<p>Ease of preparation: intermediate<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p>Active Time: 30 minutes<\/p>\n<p>Total Time: 1 hour 40 minutes<\/p>\n","parent":null,"link":"http:\/\/www.guyfieri.com\/recipes\/mexicana-meatloaf-with-cilantro-pesto-and-crispy-tortilla-strips\/","date":"2015-02-07T01:15:56","modified":"2015-02-07T01:15:56","format":"standard","slug":"mexicana-meatloaf-with-cilantro-pesto-and-crispy-tortilla-strips","guid":"http:\/\/www.guyfieri.com\/?post_type=recipes&#038;p=4846","excerpt":"<p>Preheat the oven to 350 degrees F. the oven to 400 degrees F.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Prepare the Tapenade:<\/strong> In a food processor, combine the olives, red peppers, raisins, orange zest, tarragon, parsley, capers and black pepper.<\/p>\n<p>Pulse 6-7 times until just combined and rough chopped.<\/p>\n<p>Pour in the olive oil and pulse 2-3 times more to mix together. The mixture should be smooth and loose but textured still.<\/p>\n<p>Cover and set aside in fridge until ready to use.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p><strong>Prepare the Cauliflower:<\/strong> Preheat the grill to medium.<\/p>\n<p>Remove the outer green leaves from the cauliflower, leaving the core in tact. Place the cauliflower on a cutting board on its base. Using a sharp knife (serrated works well), slice down the center creating two even halves. Carefully slice 1-inch steaks out of each piece. Repeat the process with the other head of cauliflower to end up with 4 cauliflower steaks.<\/p>\n<p>Generously coat the steaks with oil on both sides and season with salt and pepper. Place on hot grill and cook for 5 minutes on each side until golden brown and well marked.<\/p>\n<p>Remove the steaks from the grill and place on a foil lined baking sheet.<\/p>\n<p>In a small bowl, combine the parsley, panko, garlic, chile and parmesan cheese. Season with salt and pepper.<\/p>\n<p>Sprinkle breading on top of each cauliflower steak and finish with a light drizzle of olive oil which will help the browning process.<\/p>\n<p>Place in the oven for 10 to 12 minutes until golden brown on top. seconds.<\/p>\n<p><strong>To assemble the southwest lobster roll:<\/strong> Place the avocado slices on the bottom bun halves.<\/p>\n<p>Remove the lobster tails from the shells and take 2 pieces of Dutch oven with 3 cups canola oil to 300 degrees F.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p><strong>For the seasoning:\u00a0<\/strong>In a small mixing bowl combine the ancho powder, smoked paprika, cumin, onion powder, granulated garlic, sugar, salt, pepper, and superfine sugar. Store in airtight container.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p><strong>For the fries:\u00a0<\/strong>In a large bowl filled with 8 cups of water and the white vinegar soak the yucca fries for 30 minutes to remove the starch.<\/p>\n<p>In a large stock pot bring 6 quarts of water with 1 tablespoon of salt to a boil, add the yucca fries and cook until tender and almost translucent, about 6 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Remove the yucca fries from the water with a slotted spoon and place onto a clean towel to absorb the water; allow the yucca fries to cool.<\/p>\n<p>Divide the yucca fries into 3 batches, place the first batch into the 300 degrees oil.<\/p>\n<p>Blanch for 2 minutes, remove from oil, and drain excess fat.\u00a0Repeat this 2 more times.<\/p>\n<p>Bring the canola oil up to 360 degrees F. In batches, add the yucca fries to the canola and fry until golden brown and crispy, about 3 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Remove from the hot oil with a slotted spoon, place on paper towel lined plate.\u00a0Repeat this process 2 more times.<\/p>\n<p>Season hot yucca fries with the southwest fry seasoning.<\/p>\n<p>Serve immediately.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p><strong>Yield:<\/strong> serves 4 to 6<\/p>\n<p><strong>Time:<\/strong> 45 minutes<\/p>\n","parent":null,"link":"http:\/\/www.guyfieri.com\/recipes\/yucca-fries-with-southwest-fry-seasoning\/","date":"2015-01-30T06:03:40","modified":"2015-01-30T06:04:05","format":"standard","slug":"yucca-fries-with-southwest-fry-seasoning","guid":"http:\/\/www.guyfieri.com\/?post_type=recipes&#038;p=5468","excerpt":"<p>Preheat Dutch oven with 3 cups canola oil to 300 degrees F. &nbsp; For the seasoning:\u00a0In a small mixing bowl combine the ancho powder, smoked paprika, cumin, onion powder, granulated garlic, sugar, salt, pepper, and superfine sugar. Oysters Rockefeller with Baby Spinach Bacon Fondue","status":"publish","type":"recipes","author":{"ID":9,"username":"becca","name":"Becca Pariser","first_name":"Becca","last_name":"Pariser","nickname":"becca","slug":"becca","URL":"","avatar":"http:\/\/1.gravatar.com\/avatar\/a64ab12f1a2e03c57e5ed3daae0819d0?s=96","description":"","registered":"2014-01-22T18:04:20+00:00","meta":{"links":{"self":"http:\/\/www.guyfieri.com\/wp-json\/users\/9","archives":"http:\/\/www.guyfieri.com\/wp-json\/users\/9\/posts"}}},"content":"<p>Preheat the grill to medium-high heat.<\/p>\n<p>Heat 4 tablespoons of butter with shallots, garlic, bacon, and salt in a large saute pan.<\/p>\n<p>Saute until the shallots are translucent and the bacon is crispy, about 6 to 8 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Add the flour and mix together well to make a roux. Stirring frequently, cook the roux until it smells nutty, about 4 to 5 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Away from the burner deglaze the roux with the anise liquor, place the pan back on the burner being careful, as the anise liquor will flame up.<\/p>\n<p>Add the heavy cream and stir to incorporate.<\/p>\n<p>Bring the mixture to a boil then reduce to a simmer, about 5 to 7 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Stir in the baby spinach, black pepper, red pepper flakes, and nutmeg, and bring back to a boil.<\/p>\n<p>Once at a boil, immediately reduce to a simmer, about 4 to 6 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Cook until the spinach has release its liquid, and spinach has softened.<\/p>\n<p>Over medium heat cook the mixture down to a fondue like thickness, about 6 to 8 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Remove from the heat and reserve to the side.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p>Melt the remaining 4 tablespoons of butter in a small saute pan.<\/p>\n<p>Once melted remove from the heat and incorporate the seasoned bread crumbs, reserve to the side.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p>Turn broiler on.<\/p>\n<p>Take the oysters and place on the pre-heated to high grill, cook the oysters until the shell just \u201cPOPS\u201d open, about 3 minutes, remove the oysters from the grill.<\/p>\n<p>Take an oyster knife and pry open the top shell, scraping the oyster knife around the top of the shell to loosen the oyster from the shell. BE CAREFUL.<\/p>\n<p>Once the top shell has been removed discard, with the oyster knife scrape the knife under the bottom of the oyster to remove from the bottom shell, leaving the oyster \u201con the half shell\u201d, repeat this to the remaining 17 oysters.<\/p>\n<p>Place the rock salt evenly onto a baking tray that fits 18 large oysters.<\/p>\n<p>Evenly place the oysters, shell down, onto the rock salt, making sure to press the oyster shells into the salt.<\/p>\n<p>Evenly spoon the baby spinach bacon fondue on top of the oysters, now take and evenly place the grated cheeses on top of the fondue.<\/p>\n<p>Evenly sprinkle the buttered seasoned bread crumbs on top of the cheese.<\/p>\n<p>Place the baking tray with the oysters into the preheated broiler and cook until the oysters are bubbly and the bread crumbs are toasted , about 4 to 5 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Remove from the broiler and place onto a cooling rack.<\/p>\n<p>Serve the oysters immediately.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p><strong>Yield:<\/strong> serves 4 to 6<\/p>\n<p><strong>Time:<\/strong> 45 minutes<\/p>\n","parent":null,"link":"http:\/\/www.guyfieri.com\/recipes\/grilled-oysters-rockefeller-with-baby-spinach-bacon-fondue\/","date":"2015-01-30T05:59:26","modified":"2015-01-30T05:59:26","format":"standard","slug":"grilled-oysters-rockefeller-with-baby-spinach-bacon-fondue","guid":"http:\/\/www.guyfieri.com\/?post_type=recipes&#038;p=5467","excerpt":"<p>Preheat the grill to medium-high heat. reduced to 1\/2 cup, about 45 minutes, reserve to the side.<\/p>\n<p>Season the New York strip steaks with the salt and pepper and allow to sit for 15 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Place the New York strip steaks on the grill, evenly spaced, grill the steaks for 2 1\/2 minutes and rotate a quarter turn to the side for each steak and cook another 2 1\/2 minutes. This creates a cross-hatch sear marks on the steak.<\/p>\n<p>Flip the steaks over and repeat the same cooking process, about 10 minutes in total.<\/p>\n<p>Remove the New York strip steak from the grill and place on a baking tray, allow the steaks to rest for 4 to 5 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p>Add 2 tablespoon of the butter, shallots and cracked 5 peppercorn blend in a medium saucepan over medium heat.\u00a0Cook the shallots and peppercorns until the peppercorns are fragrant and the butter has started to bubble.<\/p>\n<p>Away from the flame add the brandy and the red wine, place back on the burner and allow the brandy and wine to flame up, being careful not to burn yourself.<\/p>\n<p>Add the reduced beef stock and heavy whipping cream, bring all back to a boil and immediately reduce to a simmer, allow the liquid to reduce by two-thirds, about 8 to 10 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Prior to serving whisk in the remaining 2 tablespoons of butter to the sauce and remove from the heat.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p>With a sharp knife slice the steak into 1\/2 inch thick slices on an angle.<\/p>\n<p>Place each sliced New York strip steak steaks on a large serving platter.<\/p>\n<p>Garnish the New York strip steaks by spooning the reserved five peppercorn sauce over the steaks and sprinkle with the minced parsley.<\/p>\n<p>Serve immediately.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p><strong>Yield:<\/strong> serves 4 to 6<\/p>\n<p><strong>Time:<\/strong> 1 hour<\/p>\n","parent":null,"link":"http:\/\/www.guyfieri.com\/recipes\/grilled-new-york-strip-steak-with-five-peppercorn-sauce\/","date":"2015-01-30T05:55:32","modified":"2015-01-30T05:55:32","format":"standard","slug":"grilled-new-york-strip-steak-with-five-peppercorn-sauce","guid":"http:\/\/www.guyfieri.com\/?post_type=recipes&#038;p=5466","excerpt":"<p>Preheat the grill to medium-high heat. Pariser","first_name":"Becca","last_name":"Pariser","nickname":"becca","slug":"becca","URL":"","avatar":"http:\/\/1.gravatar.com\/avatar\/a64ab12f1a2e03c57e5ed3daae0819d0?s=96","description":"","registered":"2014-01-22T18:04:20+00:00","meta":{"links":{"self":"http:\/\/www.guyfieri.com\/wp-json\/users\/9","archives":"http:\/\/www.guyfieri.com\/wp-json\/users\/9\/posts"}}},"content":"<p><strong>Makes:<\/strong> 6 servings<\/p>\n<p><strong>Time:<\/strong> 2 hours 30 minutes<\/p>\n<p><b>You&#8217;ll Need:\u00a0<\/b>Grill, Food Processor or Blender, Toothpicks<\/p>\n<p><b>Prep-Ahead Tip:<\/b> Brine and wrap the chicken thighs the night before. Transport in an airtight container in an iced cooler to the tailgate. Make the peri peri a day in advance, which allows the flavors to meld together nicely.<\/p>\n<p><strong>To make the brine:<\/strong> In a large container, combine 2 quarts water, the salt, sugar, garlic, orange and thyme. Submerge the chicken thighs in the brine and refrigerate for 2 hours.<\/p>\n<p>In a medium skillet over medium heat, cook the bacon for 3 to 5 minutes, until barely colored and still pliable. Set aside.<\/p>\n<p>Meanwhile,\u00a0<strong>make the peri peri sauce:<\/strong> Roast the chilies and red pepper at 400F for 20 minutes (or over an open flame if camping).<\/p>\n<p>Once cool enough to handle, chop finely.<\/p>\n<p>Meanwhile, sweat the onions and garlic in canola oil for 5 to 8 minutes, until softened.<\/p>\n<p>Put the chopped peppers, onion, garlic, salt, paprika, red pepper flakes, and tomato paste in a food processor and pulse until combined.<\/p>\n<p>Add the vinegar and lime juice and pulse again to incorporate. With the food processor running, stream the olive oil in slowly to achieve a smooth puree (similar to the texture of ketchup). Fold in the chopped cilantro.<\/p>\n<p>Preheat a grill to medium heat and wipe the grates with an oiled paper towel.<\/p>\n<p>Remove the chicken from the brine, pat dry and season lightly with salt and pepper.<\/p>\n<p>Wrap each thigh in 2 pieces of bacon, securing with a toothpick.<\/p>\n<p>Grill the chicken, turning once, for 10 to 15 minutes per side, basting with the sauce for the final 5 to 8 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Remove the toothpicks and serve with extra peri peri sauce.<\/p>\n","parent":null,"link":"http:\/\/www.guyfieri.com\/recipes\/brazilian-bacon-wrapped-chicken-thighs-with-peri-peri-sauce\/","date":"2015-01-29T06:31:13","modified":"2015-01-29T06:31:13","format":"standard","slug":"brazilian-bacon-wrapped-chicken-thighs-with-peri-peri-sauce","guid":"http:\/\/www.guyfieri.com\/?post_type=recipes&#038;p=5452","excerpt":"<p>Makes: 6 servings Time: 2 hours 30 minutes You&#8217;ll Need:\u00a0Grill, Food Processor or Blender, Toothpicks Prep-Ahead Tip: Brine and wrap the chicken thighs the night before. Transport in an airtight container in an iced cooler to the tailgate. Make the peri peri a day in advance, which allows the flavors to meld together nicely. Maria Tri-Tip and Achiote Oil","status":"publish","type":"recipes","author":{"ID":9,"username":"becca","name":"Becca Pariser","first_name":"Becca","last_name":"Pariser","nickname":"becca","slug":"becca","URL":"","avatar":"http:\/\/1.gravatar.com\/avatar\/a64ab12f1a2e03c57e5ed3daae0819d0?s=96","description":"","registered":"2014-01-22T18:04:20+00:00","meta":{"links":{"self":"http:\/\/www.guyfieri.com\/wp-json\/users\/9","archives":"http:\/\/www.guyfieri.com\/wp-json\/users\/9\/posts"}}},"content":"<p><strong>Santa Maria Tri-Tip<\/strong><\/p>\n<p><strong>Makes:<\/strong> 6 servings<\/p>\n<p><strong>Time:<\/strong> 8 hours<\/p>\n<p><strong>You\u2019ll need:<\/strong> Grill, instant-read thermometer<\/p>\n<p><strong>Prep-Ahead Tip:<\/strong> Achiote oil can be made weeks in advance.<\/p>\n<p>Marinate and wrap the tri-tip at least 1 day before.<\/p>\n<p>Combine the granulated garlic and pepper in a small\u00a0bowl and set aside. Mince the\u00a0garlic and slowly incorporate the salt and sugar, alternating, to create a paste. Add the Achiote Oil and mix well. Be careful; this oil will stain.<\/p>\n<p>Rinse the roast under cold water and pat it dry. Rub with the garlic-achiote paste,\u00a0evenly coating the meat. Sprinkle evenly with the granulated garlic and pepper mixture\u00a0and wrap tightly in plastic.<\/p>\n<p>Refrigerate for at least\u00a024 hours and up to 48 hours.<\/p>\n<p>Remove the wrap and allow the roast to come up in temperature while you preheat a\u00a0well-oiled grill to medium-high heat. (If available, cook on grills over an open pit of red\u00a0oak, which is traditional Santa Maria style).<\/p>\n<p>Place the tri-tip on the grill and cook for 9 minutes,\u00a0flip, cook for 9 minutes more on\u00a0second side, and check the temperature with an instant-read thermometer. Once it\u00a0reaches 90\u00b0F, increase the grill heat to high and sear\u00a0all sides of the roast, making sure\u00a0to get a nice crust on it about 3 to 4 minutes each side.<\/p>\n<p>Set it aside to rest for 10 to 15\u00a0minutes, loosely covered with aluminum foil.<\/p>\n<p>Slice the tri-tip across the grain into thin (1\u20448-inch)\u00a0pieces, drizzle any juices that have\u00a0accumulated back onto the sliced meat, and serve immediately.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p><strong>Achiote Oil<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>In a small saucepan over medium-high heat, toast the seeds for 2 to 3 minutes. Add the\u00a0oil, reduce the heat to low, and cook for 5 to 6 minutes. The oil will become bright\u00a0orange. Immediately remove from the heat, cool, and strain. Store the oil in a glass\u00a0container in the refrigerator. it\u2019s easier\u00a0to slice nice and thin. Make the jus\u00a0ahead of time, and when you reheat it you can fortify it with any off-cuts from the beef.<\/p>\n<p>Garlic butter and horseradish mayo can be made a day or\u00a0two in advance. Simply store\u00a0them in the fridge or cooler in an airtight container<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p><strong>To make the jus<\/strong>, set a medium saucepan over medium heat.<\/p>\n<p>Saute the shallots and\u00a0garlic in the olive oil and butter until caramelized\u00a0lightly, 7 to 8 minutes. Add the flour\u00a0and mix together to form a loose paste. Drain it, pat it dry, and stuff with\u00a0andouille before you transport it to your tailgate,\u00a0so all you have to do on-site is unwrap it and grill it.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p>To prepare the brine, bring 6 cups water, the salt, sugar, peppercorns, garlic, thyme, bay leaves\u00a0and\u00a0onion to a simmer in a medium pot over medium heat.<\/p>\n<p>Stir until the sugar and salt have completely\u00a0dissolved. Remove from the heat and add the ice cubes to cool.<\/p>\n<p>Place the pork loin in large freezer bag (or large plastic container with a lid). Pour the brine in\u00a0to the\u00a0freezer bag, submerging the roast completely, seal,\u00a0and set aside for 2 hours.<\/p>\n<p>Preheat the grill and set up two zones\u2014one hot for searing and another medium for cooking through.<\/p>\n<p>Using the tip of a paring knife, pierce the casing of the sausage all over (this will ensure the flavor of\u00a0the sausage goes into the pork as it cooks). Remove\u00a0the pork from the brine and pat it dry with paper\u00a0towels. Using a clean honing steel, poke a hole into the center of the loin lengthwise and work it all\u00a0the\u00a0way through so it creates a cavity. Insert the sausage into the cavity so that it sits neatly within the roast.<\/p>\n<p>Season the roast with salt, pepper, granulated garlic, paprika, and cumin.<\/p>\n<p>Wipe down the grates of the grill with oil-blotted towels. Place the roast on the hot part of the grill\u00a0and sear fat side down, 3 to 4 minutes, and then on\u00a0each of the three other sides. Transfer the roast\u00a0to\u00a0the cooler part of the grill (indirect heat) and cook until the internal temperature hits 165\u00b0F on an\u00a0instant-read thermometer, 45 to 55 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Set the\u00a0roast on a platter and tent with foil. Allow it to\u00a0rest\u00a0for 15 minutes before carving into thick slices.<\/p>\n<p>Served drizzled with juices from the platter and the\u00a0Creole mustard.<\/p>\n","parent":null,"link":"http:\/\/www.guyfieri.com\/recipes\/andouille-stuffed-pork-loin-with-creole-mustard\/","date":"2015-01-24T19:09:44","modified":"2015-01-24T19:28:16","format":"standard","slug":"andouille-stuffed-pork-loin-with-creole-mustard","guid":"http:\/\/www.guyfieri.com\/?post_type=recipes&#038;p=5428","excerpt":"<p>Makes: 6 to 8 servings Time: 3 hours You\u2019ll need: Grill with lid, large freezer bag, honing steel, instant-read meat thermometer Prep-Ahead Tip: Prepare and brine the pork loin the\u00a0morning of. Store in an airtight container.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p><strong>Garlic Butter:<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>In a medium sauce pan over medium heat, add the butter and garlic, melt the butter and cook the garlic until garlic becomes fragrant, 5 to 6 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Add the parsley, mix well.<\/p>\n<p>Reserve to the side in a small bowl.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p><strong>Donkey Sauce:<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>In a small mixing bowl combine the mayonnaise, roasted garlic, Worcestershire sauce, yellow mustard, salt and pepper, mix well until smooth. Cover and reserve.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p><strong>Burger:<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>In a large cast iron skillet over medium-high heat, place strips of applewood bacon, into the skillet, cook the bacon until crispy and brown on both sides.<\/p>\n<p>Remove and place onto a paper towel line plate.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p>Form each part of the ground beef into a loose ball and create 4-inch patties.<\/p>\n<p>Take 1 patty and evenly place 2 ounces of Point Reyes blue cheese on top of the patty.<\/p>\n<p>Place another patty over top of the Point Reyes blue cheese, gently seal the edges and form into a patty, about 4 inches wide and 1 1\/2 inches thick.<\/p>\n<p>Repeat with the remaining patties to form four 4-inch patties.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p>Season the patties on both sides equally with the blackening spice.<\/p>\n<p>Place the patties on the grill spaced 3 inches apart to prevent flare ups.<\/p>\n<p>Grill the burger patties to develop a crust on the first side, about 3 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Flip over and cook on the second side to develop the crust on that side, 2 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Top the burger patties with 2 slices of bacon in an X formation, top each with 1 ounce each of the remaining point reyes blue cheese.<\/p>\n<p>Place a piece aluminum foil pan over top of the burger patties to melt the blue cheese, about 30 seconds.<\/p>\n<p>Once melted remove the burger patties to a serving tray to rest.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p>Brush the cut sides of the brioche buns lightly with the garlic butter.<\/p>\n<p>Toast the buns on the grill for 5 to 10 seconds until golden and crisp.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p><strong>To assemble the black and blue burger:<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>Smear the donkey sauce on the cut sides of both bun halves.<\/p>\n<p>Layer the bases with the pickle slices, onion slices, and the burger patties.<\/p>\n<p>Top the burger patties with tomato slices then sliced lettuce, place the top half of the buns on top.<\/p>\n<p>Place a wooden 5 inch skewer through the top of each burger.<\/p>\n<p>Place burgers on a large platter to serve.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p><strong>Yield:<\/strong>\u00a04 servings<\/p>\n<p><strong>Prep Time:<\/strong>\u00a030 minutes<\/p>\n<p><strong>Cook Time:<\/strong>\u00a015 minutes<\/p>\n<p><strong>Ease of preparation:<\/strong>\u00a0easy<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p><strong>Active Time:<\/strong>\u00a030 minutes<\/p>\n<p><strong>Total Time:<\/strong>\u00a045 minutes<\/p>\n","parent":null,"link":"http:\/\/www.guyfieri.com\/recipes\/black-and-blue-burger\/","date":"2015-01-24T09:00:52","modified":"2015-01-24T18:24:32","format":"standard","slug":"black-and-blue-burger","guid":"http:\/\/www.guyfieri.com\/?post_type=recipes&#038;p=5405","excerpt":"<p>Preheat BBQ Short Ribs","status":"publish","type":"recipes","author":{"ID":9,"username":"becca","name":"Becca Pariser","first_name":"Becca","last_name":"Pariser","nickname":"becca","slug":"becca","URL":"","avatar":"http:\/\/1.gravatar.com\/avatar\/a64ab12f1a2e03c57e5ed3daae0819d0?s=96","description":"","registered":"2014-01-22T18:04:20+00:00","meta":{"links":{"self":"http:\/\/www.guyfieri.com\/wp-json\/users\/9","archives":"http:\/\/www.guyfieri.com\/wp-json\/users\/9\/posts"}}},"content":"<p>*if you don\u2019t have a pressure cooker you can do this in a large Dutch oven and cook for 2 1\/2 hours in the oven at 350 degrees F. If you don\u2019t have a large pressure cooker, you can sear the short ribs in a large cast iron pan before building in the pressure cooker. Deglaze with the bottle of wine and add the drippings to the pressure cooker also.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p>Heat the pressure cooker over medium-high heat and add olive oil.<\/p>\n<p>Season the short ribs with 1 teaspoon each of the salt and pepper.<\/p>\n<p>Add the oil to the pressure cooker, when hot add the short ribs and sear on all sides, 4 to 6 minutes, remove from the pressure cooking and reserve.<\/p>\n<p>Lower the heat to medium and add the onions, celery, carrots, garlic and herbs, lightly caramelize the vegetables, 6 to 8 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>There should be a fond on the bottom of the pan (tasty bits from searing ribs) add the bottle of red wine and the chicken stock, with a wooden spoon scrape the bottom of the pressure cooker to get the fond into the sauce, let the wine reduce for 6 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Add the short ribs back to the pressure cooker, stir well, add the pressure cooker lid, line up arrows, keep on medium-high heat while it pressurizes, then release and reduce heat to low for 45 minutes to 1 hour.<\/p>\n<p>Remove the pressure cooker from the stove, wait for the pressure to release, carefully remove the pressure cooker lid.<\/p>\n<p>Remove the short ribs to a plate, reserve to the side.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p>Strain the cooking liquid from the pressure cooker into a small sauce pan over medium-high heat and reduce by half, about 15 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Meanwhile, in a separate saute pan add the BBQ sauce, red wine vinegar, brown sugar, red pepper flakes, hot sauce, remaining salt and black pepper, whisk together well.<\/p>\n<p>Bring sauce to a simmer.<\/p>\n<p>Add the reduced cooking liquid to the BBQ sauce mixture and cook for another 5 minutes until thickened.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p>Place the short ribs on the grill, baste with the BBQ sauce.<\/p>\n<p>Cook 2 to 3 minutes on each side until they have started to caramelize, basting each time with the BBQ sauce liberally.<\/p>\n<p>Remove the short ribs to a cutting board, allow to rest 5 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p>Serve the BBQ short ribs over a bed of Roasted Red Pepper Polenta, drizzle more BBQ sauce and garnish with sliced scallions, if Once at a boil, turn off the heat and add the ice cubes.<\/p>\n<p>Place the turkey and brine into a large resealable gallon plastic bag.<\/p>\n<p>Refrigerate, brining the chicken, for 1 hour.<\/p>\n<p>Remove from the brine and pat dry with paper towels.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p><strong>Prepare the turkey:<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>Add the thyme, rosemary, parsley, garlic, meyer lemon zest, extra virgin olive oil, salt and black pepper in a small mixing bowl.<\/p>\n<p>Mix well to combine, reserve to the side.<\/p>\n<p>Take the brined turkey and rub all over with the herb olive oil mixture until completely covered.<\/p>\n<p>Place seasoned turkey in a large cast iron skillet and place into a preheated 425 degrees F oven for 15 minutes. After 15 minutes reduce the heat to 300 degrees and cook until the internal temperature reaches 160 degrees F, about one hour 15 minutes to one hour 30 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Cover with foil if the turkey starts to get too dark.<\/p>\n<p>Remove the turkey from the oven and allow to rest for 10 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Reserve all the juices from the bottom pan. Shred the turkey when cool to the touch.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p>Preheat grill to high.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Prepare the creminis:<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>Add the creminis, extra virgin olive oil, fresh thyme leaves, salt and pepper to a medium mixing bowl and toss well to coat the creminis with the oil herbs and seasoning.<\/p>\n<p>Place the creminis on the grill. Char on all sides, 4 to 5 minutes, remove from the grill and reserve to the side.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p><strong>Prepare the garlic butter:<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>In a medium sauce pan over medium heat, add 4 tablespoons butter and garlic, melt the butter and cook the garlic until it becomes fragrant, 5 to 6 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Add the parsley, mix well.<\/p>\n<p>Reserve to the side in a small bowl.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p>In the same pan the turkey was roasted in, add 2 tablespoons butter and all of the flour, whisk together to make a roux and cook for 5 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Add the white wine to the roux while stirring, add the cremini mushrooms and the chicken stock.<\/p>\n<p>Bring to a boil and reduce to a simmer immediately.<\/p>\n<p>Simmer the gravy for 12 to 15 minutes, reducing the liquid by half.<\/p>\n<p>Heat 2 tablespoons butter and the shredded turkey in a large cast iron pan over medium-high heat.<\/p>\n<p>Let the turkey to crisp in the pan, 2 to 3 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Take the torpedo roll and lightly brush with the garlic butter, toast in the oven for 6 to 8 minutes until golden brown.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p><strong>For assembly:<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>Take the toasted torpedo roll and spoon on 1 tablespoon black truffle paste.<\/p>\n<p>Lay 2 ounces of the sliced truffle cheese from end to end, place 1\/4 of the crisped herb roasted turkey on top of the truffle cheese, arugula, spoon 2 tablespoons of the gravy over the roasted turkey.<\/p>\n<p>Repeat this to the remaining rolls.<\/p>\n<p>Serve immediately with extra the veggie slaw:<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>In a small bowl, combine the lemon zest and juice, the olive oil, salt and Aleppo or red pepper flakes.\u00a0Whisk well, and set aside.<\/p>\n<p>In a medium mixing bowl add the romaine, red onion, red pepper, cucumber, cherry tomatoes, parsley and mint, mix together until well combined.<\/p>\n<p>Pour the lemon dressing over the slaw, toss to thoroughly coat, being careful not to bruise the lettuce.<\/p>\n<p>Serve.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p>Preheat wok turned dome side up, placed over burner on medium heat<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p><strong>Flatbread:<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>Divide the dough into 3 equal parts.<\/p>\n<p>Oil and set aside at room temperature until it can be rolled out easily, about 30 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Flatten the dough balls into circles and with a floured rolling pin, roll the dough into 2 large circles, about 12 to 14 inches in diameter.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p>In a small mixing bowl combine 4 tablespoons of olive oil and the za\u2019atar, reserve to the side.<\/p>\n<p>Season the pre-heated wok with 1\/2 of the remaining olive oil.<\/p>\n<p>Place the first flatbread on top of the domed wok surface, this will start to cook immediately, brush the flat bread with 1\/2 of the reserved olive oil and za\u2019atar mixture over the flat bread.<\/p>\n<p>Spread evenly 1\/4 of an inch from the edges.<\/p>\n<p>Cook the flat bread until just lightly brown on the bottom.<\/p>\n<p>Remove the flat bread from the wok and place on a flat surface, repeat this method to the remaining flatbread.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p>Add the veggie slaw to each flatbread and garnish with goat cheese. Roll the flatbread like a burrito, cut in half and serve. the lamb kofta patties to develop a crust on the first side, about 3 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Flip over and cook on the second side to develop the crust on that side, 2 minutes, or until cooked to deep cast iron skillet with canola oil to 350 degrees F.<\/p>\n<p>Take the cabbage, remove the bruised outer leaves, cut the cabbage in half through the core to the top, separate the halves, remove the core with a V cut.<\/p>\n<p>Take the core cabbage half, lay down flat and slice finely with a chef\u2019s knife, reserve to the side.<\/p>\n<p>In a medium mixing bowl add the buttermilk, mayonnaise, sour cream, garlic powder, onion powder, dry dill, paprika, chives, fresh ground pepper and salt, whisk these all together until fully incorporate together.<\/p>\n<p>Take the finely sliced cabbage and add to the bowl, mix together well, cover and refrigerate.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p><strong>Garlic Butter:<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>In a medium sauce pan over medium heat, add the butter and garlic, melt the butter and cook the garlic until garlic becomes fragrant, 5 to 6 minutes.<\/p>\n<p>Add the parsley, mix well.<\/p>\n<p>Reserve to the side in a small bowl.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p><strong>Chicken:<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>In a deep cast iron skillet preheat canola oil to 350 degrees F with a candy thermometer.<\/p>\n<p>In a medium mixing bowl add the buttermilk and sriracha sauce, mix well and reserve to the side.<\/p>\n<p>In another medium bowl add the all-purpose flour, granulated garlic, granulated onion, black pepper and salt, mix together well until combined, reserve to the side.\u00a0\u00a0 Place the cornflakes into a medium bowl and reserve to the side.<\/p>\n<p>Place a chicken tender into the seasoned flour lightly pressing the tender down to even out the fat end to the skinny end so they cook evenly, remove from the flour with your left hand and place into the sriracha buttermilk, dip lightly to cover shake off any excess and place into the cornflakes, with your right hand press the chicken tender into the cornflake crumbs until completely breaded, remove and place onto a baking tray.<\/p>\n<p>Repeat this breading process to the remaining 11 chicken tenders.<\/p>\n<p>In 2 batches place the bread chicken tenders into the preheated 350 degree canola oil, crispy fry the chicken tender until they are golden brown on both sides, about 6 to 7 minutes, remove from the oil with a slotted spoon and place onto a paper fowl lined plate to drain the excess oil.<\/p>\n<p>Repeat the frying process to the last 6 chicken tenders and reserve to the side.<\/p>\n<p>Take the slider buns and cut in half from side to side, brush each side lightly with the garlic butter.<\/p>\n<p>In a large saute pan over medium heat, in batches.<\/p>\n<p>Grill each half of the slider buns cut side down until they are golden brown, about 30 to 45 seconds, remove and set to the side.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p>To build the crispy corn flake crusted chicken sliders:<\/p>\n<p>Take the bottom of slider bun and place the slice onion, then sliced tomato, top with a crispy chicken tender, cover the tender with the buttermilk slaw, cover with the top of the slider bun.<\/p>\n<p>Repeat with the remaining 11 sliders.<\/p>\n<p>Place the crispy cornflake crusted chicken slider on a large serving platter.<\/p>\n<p>Serve immediately.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p><strong>Yield:<\/strong> serves 4 to 6<\/p>\n<p><strong>Time:<\/strong> 45 Stir everything up with a wooden spoon, scraping the brown bits from the bottom of the pan and tossing the clams to ensure they are coated well with the sausage.<\/p>\n<p>Spread grape tomatoes over top of pan, add the thyme sprigs and season with salt and pepper. Place the whole pan in the oven to bake for 10 to 12 minutes until clams pop open and the cherry tomatoes are roasted and juicy \u2013 almost falling apart.<\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n<p>While the clams are roasting, cook the pasta.
